=== Example 0 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises.


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
People in this club who perform in school talent shows often attend and are very engaged with school events.
People in this club either perform in school talent shows often or are inactive and disinterested community members.
People in this club who chaperone high school dances are not students who attend the school.
All people in this club who are inactive and disinterested members of their community chaperone high school dances.
All young children and teenagers in this club who wish to further their academic careers and educational opportunities are students who attend the school.
Bonnie is in this club and she either both attends and is very engaged with school events and is a student who attends the school or is not someone who both attends and is very engaged with school events and is not a student who attends the school.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Bonnie performs in school talent shows often.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
ANSWER: Uncertain

**Explanation:**

Let's break down the premises and see what we can deduce:

1. **Premise 1:** People in this club who perform in school talent shows often attend and are very engaged with school events.
2. **Premise 2:** People in this club either perform in school talent shows often or are inactive and disinterested community members.
3. **Premise 3:** People in this club who chaperone high school dances are not students who attend the school.
4. **Premise 4:** All people in this club who are inactive and disinterested members of their community chaperone high school dances.
5. **Premise 5:** All young children and teenagers in this club who wish to further their academic careers and educational opportunities are students who attend the school.
6. **Premise 6:** Bonnie is in this club and she either both attends and is very engaged with school events and is a student who attends the school or is not someone who both attends and is very engaged with school events and is not a student who attends the school.

From these premises, we know that:
- If Bonnie is a student who attends the school and is very engaged with school events, then she performs in school talent shows often (from Premises 1 and 2).
- However, Bonnie could also be an inactive and disinterested community member (from Premise 2), and based on Premise 4, such members must chaperone high school dances, but they do not perform in school talent shows (Premise 3).

Given the condition in Premise 6, we have two scenarios for Bonnie:
- Scenario 1: She is a student who attends the school and is very engaged with school events. In this case, she performs in school talent shows often.
- Scenario 2: She is an inactive and disinterested community member. In this case, she does not perform in school talent shows often.

Since Bonnie could fall into either of these scenarios based on the information provided, we cannot definitively conclude whether Bonnie performs in school talent shows often or not. Therefore, the answer is **Uncertain**.
Processed: Uncertain

Reference: Uncertain
========================================

=== Example 1 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises.


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
People in this club who perform in school talent shows often attend and are very engaged with school events.
People in this club either perform in school talent shows often or are inactive and disinterested community members.
People in this club who chaperone high school dances are not students who attend the school.
All people in this club who are inactive and disinterested members of their community chaperone high school dances.
All young children and teenagers in this club who wish to further their academic careers and educational opportunities are students who attend the school.
Bonnie is in this club and she either both attends and is very engaged with school events and is a student who attends the school or is not someone who both attends and is very engaged with school events and is not a student who attends the school.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Bonnie is either both a young child or teenager who wishes to further her academic career and educational opportunities and chaperones high school dances or neither is a young child nor teenager who wishes to further her academic career and educational opportunities, then Bonnie is either a student who attends the school or is an inactive and disinterested member of the community.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
ANSWER: True

Let's break down the premises and see how they relate to the conclusion:

1. **Premise 1:** People in the club who perform in school talent shows often attend and are very engaged with school events.
2. **Premise 2:** People in the club either perform in school talent shows often or are inactive and disinterested community members.
3. **Premise 3:** People in the club who chaperone high school dances are not students who attend the school.
4. **Premise 4:** All people in the club who are inactive and disinterested community members chaperone high school dances.
5. **Premise 5:** All young children and teenagers in the club who wish to further their academic careers and educational opportunities are students who attend the school.
6. **Premise 6:** Bonnie is in the club and she either:
   - both attends and is very engaged with school events and is a student who attends the school or
   - is not someone who both attends and is very engaged with school events and is not a student who attends the school.

We need to show that the conclusion holds true given these premises.

**Conclusion to Prove:**
If Bonnie is either:
- a young child or teenager who wishes to further her academic career and educational opportunities and chaperones high school dances, or
- neither a young child nor a teenager who wishes to further her academic career and educational opportunities,
then Bonnie is either:
- a student who attends the school, or
- an inactive and disinterested member of the community.

From Premises 4 and 5:
- If Bonnie is a young child or teenager who wishes to further her academic career and educational opportunities, she must be a student who attends the school (from Premise 5).
- If Bonnie is inactive and disinterested and chaperones high school dances (Premise 4), she is not a student who attends the school.

Combining Premises 3 and 4:
- If Bonnie is an inactive and disinterested member of the community, she chaperones high school dances (Premise 4).

Now consider the given conclusion conditions:

1. **Case 1:** Bonnie is a young child or teenager who wishes to further her academic career and educational opportunities and chaperones high school dances.
   - From Premise 5, she is a student who attends the school.

2. **Case 2:** Bonnie is neither a young child nor a teenager who wishes to further her academic career and educational opportunities.
   - This means she is either performing in school talent shows or is inactive and disinterested.
   - If she is performing in school talent shows (Premise 2), she is very engaged with school events and possibly a student (Premise 1).
   - If she is inactive and disinterested (Premise 4), she chaperones high school dances (Premise 4) and thus is not a student who attends the school.

Therefore, under all scenarios, the conclusion follows from the premises. Thus, the answer is **ANSWER: True**.
Processed: True

Reference: True
========================================

The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises.


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>

</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.

<PREMISES>

<PREMISES>
People in this club who perform in school talent shows often attend and are very engaged with school events.
People in this club either perform in school talent shows often or are inactive and disinterested community members.
People in this club who chaperone high school dances are not students who attend the school.
All people in this club who are inactive and disinterested members of their community chaperone high school dances.
All young children and teenagers in this club who wish to further their academic careers and educational opportunities are students who attend the school.
Bonnie is in this club and she either both attends and is very engaged with school events and is a student who attends the school or is not someone who both attends and is very engaged with school events and is not a student who attends the school.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Bonnie either chaperones high school dances or, if she does not, she performs in school talent shows often, then Bonnie is both a young child or teenager who wishes to further her academic career and educational opportunities and an inactive and disinterested member of the community.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
ANSWER: Uncertain

Let's break down the premises and see if we can derive the conclusion logically:

1. People in this club who perform in school talent shows often attend and are very engaged with school events.
2. People in this club either perform in school talent shows often or are inactive and disinterested community members.
3. People in this club who chaperone high school dances are not students who attend the school.
4. All people in this club who are inactive and disinterested members of their community chaperone high school dances.
5. All young children and teenagers in this club who wish to further their academic careers and educational opportunities are students who attend the school.
6. Bonnie is in this club and she either both attends and is very engaged with school events and is a student who attends the school or is not someone who both attends and is very engaged with school events and is not a student who attends the school.

From these premises, we can deduce that:
- If Bonnie is a student who attends the school and is very engaged with school events, then she performs in school talent shows often.
- If Bonnie is not a student who attends the school and is very engaged with school events, then she must be an inactive and disinterested community member.
- Since all people who are inactive and disinterested community members chaperone high school dances, if Bonnie is an inactive and disinterested community member, she will chaperone high school dances.

However, the conclusion states that if Bonnie either chaperones high school dances or, if she does not, she performs in school talent shows often, then Bonnie is both a young child or teenager who wishes to further her academic career and educational opportunities and an inactive and disinterested member of the community.

This conclusion combines multiple conditions and does not directly follow from the premises without additional assumptions. Specifically, the premise about Bonnie being a student who attends the school or not attending but being very engaged does not directly connect to her being a young child or teenager who wishes to further her academic career and educational opportunities.

Given the structure and the specific conditions laid out in the premises, we cannot definitively conclude that the statement in the conclusion is true based solely on the information provided. Therefore, the answer is **Uncertain**.
Processed: Uncertain

Reference: False
========================================

=== Example 3 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises.


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All employees who schedule a meeting with their customers will go to the company building today.
Everyone who has lunch in the company building schedules meetings with their customers.
Employees have lunch either in the company building or at home.
If an employee has lunch at home, they are working remotely from home.
All employees who are in other countries work remotely from home.
No managers work remotely from home.
James will appear in the company today if and only if he is a manager.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
James has lunch in the company.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
ANSWER: Uncertain

Let's break down the premises and see if we can derive the conclusion:

1. **Premises Analysis:**
   - All employees who schedule a meeting with their customers will go to the company building today.
   - Everyone who has lunch in the company building schedules meetings with their customers.
   - Employees have lunch either in the company building or at home.
   - If an employee has lunch at home, they are working remotely from home.
   - All employees who are in other countries work remotely from home.
   - No managers work remotely from home.
   - James will appear in the company today if and only if he is a manager.

2. **Possible Scenarios for James:**
   - If James is a manager, then according to the last premise, James will be in the company today. Since managers do not work remotely from home, this implies James does not have lunch at home.
   - If James is not a manager, he cannot be in the company today due to the "if and only if" condition. Therefore, if James is not in the company today, he must be working remotely from home, which means he has lunch at home.

3. **Deriving Lunch Location:**
   - If James is in the company, he must have lunch in the company because employees have lunch either in the company building or at home, and if he had lunch at home, he would be working remotely, which contradicts the fact that he is in the company.

4. **Conclusion Evaluation:**
   - The premises do not provide enough information to definitively state that James will have lunch in the company if he is in the company. It is possible that James might have lunch at home and still be in the company if he is not a manager, but this would contradict the last premise.
   
   Since the premises do not rule out the possibility that James could be in the company while having lunch at home (if he is not a manager), the conclusion that "James has lunch in the company" cannot be definitively derived from the premises.

Therefore, the answer is **ANSWER: Uncertain**.
Processed: Uncertain

Reference: Uncertain
========================================

=== Example 4 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises.


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All employees who schedule a meeting with their customers will go to the company building today.
Everyone who has lunch in the company building schedules meetings with their customers.
Employees have lunch either in the company building or at home.
If an employee has lunch at home, they are working remotely from home.
All employees who are in other countries work remotely from home.
No managers work remotely from home.
James will appear in the company today if and only if he is a manager.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
James does not have lunch in the company.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
ANSWER: True

Let's break down the premises and see how they lead to the conclusion:

1. **Premise 1**: All employees who schedule a meeting with their customers will go to the company building today.
2. **Premise 2**: Everyone who has lunch in the company building schedules meetings with their customers.
3. **Premise 3**: Employees have lunch either in the company building or at home.
4. **Premise 4**: If an employee has lunch at home, they are working remotely from home.
5. **Premise 5**: All employees who are in other countries work remotely from home.
6. **Premise 6**: No managers work remotely from home.
7. **Premise 7**: James will appear in the company today if and only if he is a manager.

From Premise 7, we know that if James appears in the company today, he must be a manager. Since no managers work remotely from home (Premise 6), this means if James were working remotely from home, he would not be appearing in the company today. 

From Premises 3 and 4, if James has lunch at home, he would be working remotely from home. Therefore, if James were working remotely from home, he would not be at the company (and thus not a manager). However, since being a manager implies James could be at the company, he cannot be working remotely from home if he is a manager.

By Premise 2, anyone who has lunch in the company building schedules meetings with their customers, and by Premise 1, those who schedule meetings with their customers go to the company building today. Thus, if James had lunch in the company building, he would be at the company today, which aligns with him being a manager (if he is one).

Since we know that James can only be at the company today if he is a manager, and managers do not work remotely from home, the only way for him to be at the company is if he is not working remotely from home. Given Premises 4 and 5, this means James cannot have lunch at home because that would imply he is working remotely from home.

Therefore, James must have lunch in the company to not work remotely and still be a manager, which contradicts the statement "James does not have lunch in the company." Hence, the only consistent scenario is that James does not have lunch in the company.

Thus, the conclusion "James does not have lunch in the company" is true based on the given premises.
Processed: True

Reference: Uncertain
========================================

=== Example 5 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises.


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All employees who schedule a meeting with their customers will go to the company building today.
Everyone who has lunch in the company building schedules meetings with their customers.
Employees have lunch either in the company building or at home.
If an employee has lunch at home, they are working remotely from home.
All employees who are in other countries work remotely from home.
No managers work remotely from home.
James will appear in the company today if and only if he is a manager.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If James is either a manager or in other countries,  then James does not either has lunch at home or work remotely from home. If James either has lunch at home or works remotely from home, then he is neither a manager nor does he work in other countries. [contrapositive is more natural]
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
ANSWER: True

Explanation:

To determine the validity of the conclusion, we can start by examining the contrapositive form of the statement: "If James is either a manager or in other countries, then James does not either has lunch at home or work remotely from home." The contrapositive of a statement \(P \rightarrow Q\) is \(\neg Q \rightarrow \neg P\), which is logically equivalent to the original statement.

Given premises:
1. All employees who schedule a meeting with their customers will go to the company building today.
2. Everyone who has lunch in the company building schedules meetings with their customers.
3. Employees have lunch either in the company building or at home.
4. If an employee has lunch at home, they are working remotely from home.
5. All employees who are in other countries work remotely from home.
6. No managers work remotely from home.
7. James will appear in the company today if and only if he is a manager.

We need to consider the logical implications of these premises for the conclusion.

Let's break it down:

- If James is a manager (\(J_m\)), then he does not work remotely from home (from premise 6).
- If James is in other countries (\(J_{oc}\)), then he works remotely from home (from premise 5).

Now let's consider the contrapositive statement: "If James is either a manager or in other countries, then James does not either has lunch at home or work remotely from home."

This can be broken into two cases:
1. If James is a manager (\(J_m\)):
   - From premise 6, James does not work remotely from home.
   - Since James does not work remotely from home, he cannot have lunch at home (from premise 4).
2. If James is in other countries (\(J_{oc}\)):
   - From premise 5, James works remotely from home.
   - Since James works remotely from home, he cannot have lunch at home.

In both cases, the contrapositive holds true based on the given premises. Therefore, the conclusion is logically valid.

Hence, the answer is **ANSWER: True**.
Processed: True

Reference: True
========================================

=== Example 6 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises.


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>

<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
There are six types of wild turkeys: Eastern wild turkey, Osceola wild turkey, Gould’s wild turkey, Merriam’s wild turkey, Rio Grande wild turkey, and Ocellated wild turkey.
Tom is not an Eastern wild turkey.
Tom is not an Osceola wild turkey.
Tom is not a Gould's wild turkey.
Tom is neither a Merriam's wild turkey nor a Rio Grande wild turkey.
Tom is a wild turkey.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Tom is an Eastern wild turkey.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
ANSWER: False

Let's analyze the premises step-by-step:

1. **Premises:**
   - There are six types of wild turkeys: Eastern wild turkey, Osceola wild turkey, Gould’s wild turkey, Merriam’s wild turkey, Rio Grande wild turkey, and Ocellated wild turkey.
   - Tom is not an Eastern wild turkey.
   - Tom is not an Osceola wild turkey.
   - Tom is not a Gould's wild turkey.
   - Tom is neither a Merriam's wild turkey nor a Rio Grande wild turkey.
   - Tom is a wild turkey.

2. **Conclusion:**
   - Tom is an Eastern wild turkey.

3. **Analysis:**
   - From the premise "There are six types of wild turkeys," we know that every wild turkey must be one of these six types.
   - The premises explicitly state that Tom is a wild turkey but he is not any of the five specific types mentioned (Eastern, Osceola, Gould’s, Merriam’s, or Rio Grande).
   - Therefore, Tom must be an Ocellated wild turkey since those are the only remaining options for wild turkeys according to the premises.

4. **Final Step:**
   - The conclusion states that Tom is an Eastern wild turkey, which contradicts all the given information about Tom.

Thus, the conclusion is false.
Processed: False

Reference: False

The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises.


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.

Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>

</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.

Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A Japanese game company created the game the Legend of Zelda.
All games on the Top 10 list are made by Japanese game companies.
If a game sells more than one million copies, then it will be included in the Top 10 list.
The Legend of Zelda sold more than one million copies.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
The Legend of Zelda is on the Top 10 list.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
ANSWER: True

Let's break down the premises step-by-step:

1. **Premise:** A Japanese game company created the game the Legend of Zelda.
2. **Premise:** All games on the Top 10 list are made by Japanese game companies.
3. **Premise:** If a game sells more than one million copies, then it will be included in the Top 10 list.
4. **Premise:** The Legend of Zelda sold more than one million copies.

From premise 4, we know that The Legend of Zelda sold more than one million copies.

Using premise 3, since The Legend of Zelda sold more than one million copies, it must be included in the Top 10 list.

Premise 2 states that all games on the Top 10 list are made by Japanese game companies. Premise 1 tells us that the Legend of Zelda was created by a Japanese game company, so it fits the condition specified in premise 2.

Thus, combining these premises, we can conclude that The Legend of Zelda is on the Top 10 list.

Therefore, the conclusion "The Legend of Zelda is on the Top 10 list" is true.
Processed: True

Reference: True

If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>

All four-sided things are shapes.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
All squares are shapes.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
ANSWER: True

Let's break down the premises:

1. All squares are four-sided.
2. All four-sided things are shapes.

From these premises, we can infer the following:
- If something is a square, then it must be four-sided (by the first premise).
- If something is four-sided, then it is a shape (by the second premise).

Combining these two inferences, if something is a square, then it must be a shape. Therefore, the conclusion "All squares are shapes" logically follows from the given premises.
Processed: True

<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All rabbits that can be spotted near the campus are cute.
Some turtles can be spotted near the campus.
The only animals that can be spotted near the campus are rabbits and squirrels.
If something is skittish, then it is not calm.
All the squirrels that can be spotted near the campus are skittish.
Rockie can be spotted near the campus, and it is calm.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Rockie is a turtle.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
ANSWER: False

Let's break down the premises and see why the conclusion is false:

1. **Premises Analysis:**
   - All rabbits that can be spotted near the campus are cute.
   - Some turtles can be spotted near the campus.
   - The only animals that can be spotted near the campus are rabbits and squirrels.
   - If something is skittish, then it is not calm.
   - All the squirrels that can be spotted near the campus are skittish.
   - Rockie can be spotted near the campus, and it is calm.

2. **Logical Inferences:**
   - Since Rockie can be spotted near the campus and it is calm, it cannot be skittish (because skittish implies not calm).
   - Since all squirrels that can be spotted near the campus are skittish, Rockie cannot be a squirrel.
   - Therefore, Rockie must be a rabbit (since it can be spotted near the campus and the only other possibility would be a turtle, but no turtle can be spotted without being a squirrel or a rabbit).

3. **Conclusion Analysis:**
   - The conclusion states that "Rockie is a turtle."
   - From the premises, we deduced that Rockie must be a rabbit because it is calm and cannot be skittish.

Therefore, the conclusion that "Rockie is a turtle" is false based on the given premises.

Generation 1:
ANSWER: True

Let's break down the premises and see how they lead to the conclusion:

1. **All rabbits that can be spotted near the campus are cute.**
2. **Some turtles can be spotted near the campus.**
3. **The only animals that can be spotted near the campus are rabbits and squirrels.**
4. **If something is skittish, then it is not calm.**
5. **All the squirrels that can be spotted near the campus are skittish.**
6. **Rockie can be spotted near the campus, and it is calm.**

Thus, Rockie cannot be a turtle. The conclusion "Rockie is not a turtle" follows logically from the premises.

Therefore, the answer is **ANSWER: True**.

The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises.


<PREMISES>

All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.

</PREMISES>

</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.

Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All rabbits that can be spotted near the campus are cute.
Some turtles can be spotted near the campus.
The only animals that can be spotted near the campus are rabbits and squirrels.
If something is skittish, then it is not calm.
All the squirrels that can be spotted near the campus are skittish.
Rockie can be spotted near the campus, and it is calm.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Rockie is not both a turtle and a squirrel, then Rockie is either cute or skittish.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
ANSWER: True

**Explanation:**

1. **Premises Analysis:**
   - All rabbits that can be spotted near the campus are cute.
   - Some turtles can be spotted near the campus.
   - The only animals that can be spotted near the campus are rabbits and squirrels.
   - If something is skittish, then it is not calm.
   - All the squirrels that can be spotted near the campus are skittish.
   - Rockie can be spotted near the campus, and it is calm.

2. **Conclusion Analysis:**
   - If Rockie is not both a turtle and a squirrel, then Rockie is either cute or skittish.

3. **Logical Deduction:**
   - From the third premise, we know the only animals spotted near the campus are rabbits and squirrels.
   - Since Rockie can be spotted near the campus, Rockie must be either a rabbit or a squirrel.
   - Rockie is calm (fourth premise).
   - If something is skittish, it is not calm (fifth premise). Thus, since Rockie is calm, Rockie cannot be skittish.
   - Therefore, if Rockie is not a turtle (which leaves it as being a rabbit or a squirrel), and Rockie is not skittish (and thus not a squirrel because all squirrels that can be spotted near the campus are skittish), then Rockie must be a rabbit.
   - Since all rabbits that can be spotted near the campus are cute (first premise), Rockie, being a rabbit, is cute.
   - Hence, if Rockie is not both a turtle and a squirrel, then Rockie is cute, which satisfies the condition of being either cute or skittish (since Rockie is not skittish).

Thus, the conclusion is logically true based on the given premises.
Processed: True

Reference: True

A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>

If a Netflix show is popular, Karen will binge-watch it.
If and only if Karen binge-watches a Netflix show, she will download it.
Karen does not download "Black Mirror."
"Black Mirror" is a Netflix show.
If Karen binge-watches a Netflix show, she will share it with Lisa.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Karen will share "Black Mirror" with Lisa.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
ANSWER: False

Explanation:
- From the premises, we know that "Black Mirror" is a Netflix show and Karen does not download "Black Mirror."
- We also know that if Karen binge-watches a Netflix show, she will download it. Since Karen does not download "Black Mirror," it means she did not binge-watch "Black Mirror."
- Additionally, if Karen binge-watches a Netflix show, she will share it with Lisa. Since Karen did not binge-watch "Black Mirror," she will not share it with Lisa.

Therefore, the conclusion "Karen will share 'Black Mirror' with Lisa" is false based on the given premises.
Processed: False

=== Example 27 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises.


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All aliens are extraterrestrials.
If someone is from Mars, then they are an alien.
No extraterrestrials are human.
All highly intelligent beings from Earth are humans.
Marvin is a highly intelligent being.
Marvin is either from Earth and from Mars, or he is from neither.
If Marvin is not from Earth, then Marvin is an extraterrestrial.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Marvin is an alien.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
ANSWER: True

Let's break down the premises step by step:

1. **All aliens are extraterrestrials.**
   - This means if someone is an alien, then they are also an extraterrestrial.

2. **If someone is from Mars, then they are an alien.**
   - This means Mars inhabitants are included in the category of aliens.

3. **No extraterrestrials are human.**
   - This means extraterrestrials cannot be humans.

4. **All highly intelligent beings from Earth are humans.**
   - This means any highly intelligent being from Earth falls into the category of humans.

5. **Marvin is a highly intelligent being.**
   - From this, we can infer that if Marvin is from Earth, then Marvin is a human (since all highly intelligent beings from Earth are humans).

6. **Marvin is either from Earth and from Mars, or he is from neither.**
   - This gives us two scenarios:
     - Scenario 1: Marvin is from Earth and from Mars.
     - Scenario 2: Marvin is from neither Earth nor Mars.

7. **If Marvin is not from Earth, then Marvin is an extraterrestrial.**
   - If Marvin is not from Earth, he must be from Mars (since the only option left if he's not from Earth is Mars). Since someone from Mars is an alien, Marvin would be an extraterrestrial and thus an alien by the first premise.

Now let's consider the possible scenarios for Marvin:

- **Scenario 1:** If Marvin is from Earth, then Marvin is a human. But since Marvin is also a highly intelligent being, he must be from Earth and thus a human. No contradiction here, but no direct information that Marvin is an alien.
  
- **Scenario 2:** If Marvin is from neither Earth nor Mars, then Marvin must be an extraterrestrial by the sixth premise, and hence an alien by the first premise.

Since the scenario where Marvin could be an alien (from Mars but not Earth) aligns with the given premises, and the other scenario doesn't contradict it, we can conclude that Marvin is indeed an alien.

Therefore, the answer is **ANSWER: True**.
Processed: True

Reference: Uncertain

<PREMISES>
All aliens are extraterrestrials.
If someone is from Mars, then they are an alien.
No extraterrestrials are human.
All highly intelligent beings from Earth are humans.
Marvin is a highly intelligent being.
Marvin is either from Earth and from Mars, or he is from neither.
If Marvin is not from Earth, then Marvin is an extraterrestrial.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Marvin is neither a human nor from Mars.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
ANSWER: False

Let's break down the reasoning:

1. **Premise Analysis**:
   - All aliens are extraterrestrials.
   - If someone is from Mars, then they are an alien.
   - No extraterrestrials are human.
   - All highly intelligent beings from Earth are humans.
   - Marvin is a highly intelligent being.
   - Marvin is either from Earth and from Mars, or he is from neither.
   - If Marvin is not from Earth, then Marvin is an extraterrestrial.

2. **Conclusion**:
   - Marvin is neither a human nor from Mars.

3. **Reasoning**:
   - Since Marvin is a highly intelligent being and all highly intelligent beings from Earth are humans, Marvin cannot be from Earth if he is not a human.
   - From the premise "If Marvin is not from Earth, then Marvin is an extraterrestrial," we can deduce that if Marvin is not from Earth, he must be an extraterrestrial.
   - Since no extraterrestrials are human, if Marvin is an extraterrestrial, he is not a human.
   - Given the premise that Marvin is either from Earth and from Mars, or he is from neither, and considering Marvin cannot be from Earth if he is not a human (because he would then be a human), Marvin must be from neither Earth nor Mars.
   - If Marvin is not from Earth, he must be an extraterrestrial, but we don't have any information indicating that Marvin is specifically from Mars.
   - Therefore, Marvin could be an extraterrestrial who is not from Mars.

Since the conclusion states that Marvin is neither a human nor from Mars, and we can only definitively conclude that Marvin is not from Earth, the statement that Marvin is not from Mars is not supported by the premises. Hence, the answer is **ANSWER: False**.
Processed: False

The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises.


<PREMISES>

All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.
</PREMISES>

A worksheet is not biodegradable.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: Uncertain
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All aliens are extraterrestrials.
If someone is from Mars, then they are an alien.
No extraterrestrials are human.
All highly intelligent beings from Earth are humans.
Marvin is a highly intelligent being.
Marvin is either from Earth and from Mars, or he is from neither.
If Marvin is not from Earth, then Marvin is an extraterrestrial.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Marvin is not from Mars, then Marvin is a human.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
ANSWER: True

Let's break down the premises step-by-step to understand why the conclusion is true:

1. **Premise Analysis**:
   - All aliens are extraterrestrials.
   - If someone is from Mars, then they are an alien.
   - No extraterrestrials are human.
   - All highly intelligent beings from Earth are humans.
   - Marvin is a highly intelligent being.
   - Marvin is either from Earth and from Mars, or he is from neither.
   - If Marvin is not from Earth, then Marvin is an extraterrestrial.

2. **Determine Marvin's Origin**:
   - From the premise "Marvin is either from Earth and from Mars, or he is from neither," we know that Marvin cannot be from both Earth and Mars simultaneously. This means Marvin is either from Earth, from Mars, or from neither.

3. **Case 1: Marvin is from Earth**:
   - If Marvin is from Earth, then according to the premise "All highly intelligent beings from Earth are humans," Marvin must be a human. Therefore, Marvin cannot be an extraterrestrial.

4. **Case 2: Marvin is from Mars**:
   - If Marvin is from Mars, then by the premise "If someone is from Mars, then they are an alien," Marvin is an alien. Since all aliens are extraterrestrials (premise 1), Marvin is also an extraterrestrial. By the premise "No extraterrestrials are human," Marvin cannot be a human.

5. **Case 3: Marvin is from Neither**:
   - If Marvin is from neither Earth nor Mars, then the condition "If Marvin is not from Earth, then Marvin is an extraterrestrial" applies. Since Marvin is not from Earth, this implies that Marvin must be an extraterrestrial. Again, since all extraterrestrials cannot be human, Marvin cannot be a human.

6. **Conclusion**:
   - In all cases where Marvin is not from Mars, Marvin must either be from Earth (in which case Marvin is a human) or from neither (in which case Marvin is an extraterrestrial and cannot be a human).
   - Thus, if Marvin is not from Mars, Marvin must be from Earth, making Marvin a human.

Therefore, the conclusion "If Marvin is not from Mars, then Marvin is a human" logically follows from the premises. The correct answer is **ANSWER: True**.
Processed: True

Reference: False

Every Grand Slam champion at the mixer is a professional tennis player.
All Oscar-nominated actors at the mixer are celebrities.
All professional tennis players at the mixer are athletes.
If a person at the mixer is a celebrity, then they are well paid.
If a person at the mixer is an athlete, then they are famous.
All well-paid people at the mixer live in tax havens.
Djokovic is at the mixer: if Djokovic is a famous athlete, then Djokovic is well-paid.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Djokovic is a Grand Slam champion.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
ANSWER: Uncertain

**Explanation:**

From the premises, we can deduce the following:

1. Everyone at the mixer is either a Grand Slam champion or an Oscar-nominated actor.
2. Every Grand Slam champion at the mixer is a professional tennis player.
3. All Oscar-nominated actors at the mixer are celebrities.
4. All professional tennis players at the mixer are athletes.
5. If a person at the mixer is a celebrity, then they are well paid.
6. If a person at the mixer is an athlete, then they are famous.
7. All well-paid people at the mixer live in tax havens.
8. Djokovic is at the mixer.
9. If Djokovic is a famous athlete, then Djokovic is well-paid.

Since Djokovic is at the mixer, he is either a Grand Slam champion or an Oscar-nominated actor. We need to determine if Djokovic being a Grand Slam champion is necessarily true based on the given premises.

- If Djokovic is a Grand Slam champion, he must be a professional tennis player according to premise 2.
- If Djokovic is a professional tennis player, he is an athlete (premise 4).
- Being an athlete means he is famous (premise 6).

Now, we need to consider the implications for his well-paid status:
- Being a famous athlete means Djokovic is well-paid (from the given implication).

This means, if Djokovic is a Grand Slam champion, he is well-paid. However, the premises do not provide information that excludes the possibility that Djokovic could be an Oscar-nominated actor who is also well-paid, without being a Grand Slam champion. 

Therefore, the conclusion "Djokovic is a Grand Slam champion" cannot be definitively determined from the given premises. Thus, the answer is **ANSWER: Uncertain**.
Processed: Uncertain

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Real Madrid ranks higher than Barcelona.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: True
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
Everyone at the mixer is a Grand Slam champion or an Oscar-nominated actor.
Every Grand Slam champion at the mixer is a professional tennis player.
All Oscar-nominated actors at the mixer are celebrities.
All professional tennis players at the mixer are athletes.
If a person at the mixer is a celebrity, then they are well paid.
If a person at the mixer is an athlete, then they are famous.
All well-paid people at the mixer live in tax havens.
Djokovic is at the mixer: if Djokovic is a famous athlete, then Djokovic is well-paid.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Djokovic lives in a tax haven.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
ANSWER: True

**Explanation:**

1. **Premise Analysis:**
   - Everyone at the mixer is a Grand Slam champion or an Oscar-nominated actor.
   - Every Grand Slam champion at the mixer is a professional tennis player.
   - All Oscar-nominated actors at the mixer are celebrities.
   - All professional tennis players at the mixer are athletes.
   - If a person at the mixer is a celebrity, then they are well paid.
   - If a person at the mixer is an athlete, then they are famous.
   - All well-paid people at the mixer live in tax havens.
   - Djokovic is at the mixer.
   - If Djokovic is a famous athlete, then Djokovic is well-paid.

2. **Determine Djokovic's Identity:**
   - Djokovic is at the mixer.
   - Since everyone at the mixer is either a Grand Slam champion or an Oscar-nominated actor, Djokovic must be one of these.
   - If Djokovic were an Oscar-nominated actor:
     - He would be a celebrity (premise 3).
     - Hence, he would be well-paid (premise 5).
     - If he is well-paid, he lives in a tax haven (premise 7).

3. **Alternative Path for Djokovic:**
   - If Djokovic is a Grand Slam champion:
     - He would be a professional tennis player (premise 2).
     - Hence, he would be an athlete (premise 4).
     - If he is an athlete, he is famous (premise 6).
     - Being famous implies he could be well-paid.
     - If he is well-paid, he lives in a tax haven (premise 7).

4. **Conclusion:**
   - Regardless of whether Djokovic is a Grand Slam champion or an Oscar-nominated actor, the path leads to him being well-paid.
   - Therefore, Djokovic lives in a tax haven.

Thus, the conclusion "Djokovic lives in a tax haven" is logically derived from the premises, making the answer **ANSWER: True**.
Processed: True

Reference: True

All professional tennis players at the mixer are athletes.
If a person at the mixer is a celebrity, then they are well paid.
If a person at the mixer is an athlete, then they are famous.
All well-paid people at the mixer live in tax havens.
Djokovic is at the mixer: if Djokovic is a famous athlete, then Djokovic is well-paid.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Djokovic does not live in a tax haven.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
ANSWER: False

Let's break down the premises and see how they apply to Djokovic:

1. **Everyone at the mixer is a Grand Slam champion or an Oscar-nominated actor.**
2. **Every Grand Slam champion at the mixer is a professional tennis player.**
3. **All Oscar-nominated actors at the mixer are celebrities.**
4. **All professional tennis players at the mixer are athletes.**
5. **If a person at the mixer is a celebrity, then they are well paid.**
6. **If a person at the mixer is an athlete, then they are famous.**
7. **All well-paid people at the mixer live in tax havens.**
8. **Djokovic is at the mixer: if Djokovic is a famous athlete, then Djokovic is well-paid.**

From these premises, we can infer:
- Since Djokovic is at the mixer, he must be either a Grand Slam champion or an Oscar-nominated actor.
- If Djokovic is a Grand Slam champion, he is a professional tennis player.
- Therefore, if Djokovic is a Grand Slam champion, he is an athlete.
- If Djokovic is an athlete, he is famous.
- Since Djokovic is a Grand Slam champion (and thus a professional tennis player and an athlete), and if Djokovic is famous, he is well-paid.

Now, let's consider the possibility that Djokovic is well-paid:
- If Djokovic is well-paid, he lives in a tax haven according to premise 7.

Given this chain of reasoning, if Djokovic is an athlete (which he is, being a Grand Slam champion), he would be well-paid and therefore live in a tax haven. Thus, the statement "Djokovic does not live in a tax haven" is false based on the premises provided.
Processed: False

All of Zaha Hadid's design styles that Max adores have interesting geometries.
No brutalist buildings that Max adores have interesting geometries.
Every style that Max adores is either Zaha Hadid's design style or Kelly Wearstler's design style.
All of Kelly Wearstler's design styles that Max adores are evocative.
All of Kelly Wearstler's design styles that Max adores are dreamy.
If a design by Max that he adores has interesting geometries, then the design is a brutalist building and evocative.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A design by Max is a brutalist building.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
ANSWER: Uncertain

**Reasoning:**

Let's analyze the premises step-by-step:

1. **Premise Analysis:**
   - All of Zaha Hadid's design styles that Max adores have interesting geometries.
   - No brutalist buildings that Max adores have interesting geometries.
   - Every style that Max adores is either Zaha Hadid's design style or Kelly Wearstler's design style.
   - All of Kelly Wearstler's design styles that Max adores are evocative.
   - All of Kelly Wearstler's design styles that Max adores are dreamy.
   - If a design by Max that he adores has interesting geometries, then the design is a brutalist building and evocative.

2. **Conclusion Analysis:**
   - We need to determine if "A design by Max is a brutalist building" can be concluded based on the given premises.

3. **Logical Implications:**
   - From premise 1 and premise 4, we know that all of Kelly Wearstler's design styles that Max adores are evocative (and therefore not brutalist).
   - From premise 2, no brutalist buildings that Max adores have interesting geometries.
   - From premise 6, if a design by Max that he adores has interesting geometries, then it must be both a brutalist building and evocative. However, since no brutalist buildings Max adores have interesting geometries (premise 2), this implies no such brutalist building exists for Max.
   - Therefore, for a design to have interesting geometries and be adored by Max, it would have to be a brutalist building (premise 6). But since brutalist buildings with interesting geometries do not exist according to premise 2, it follows that no brutalist building can be adored by Max.

Since we cannot derive a brutalist building being adored by Max from the premises, and thus cannot definitively conclude that any brutalist building exists among the designs Max adores, the statement "A design by Max is a brutalist building" is **uncertain**.
Processed: Uncertain

Reference: Uncertain

All of Kelly Wearstler's design styles that Max adores are evocative.
All of Kelly Wearstler's design styles that Max adores are dreamy.
If a design by Max that he adores has interesting geometries, then the design is a brutalist building and evocative.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A design by Max is evocative and dreamy.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
ANSWER: True

Explanation:

1. All of Zaha Hadid's design styles that Max adores have interesting geometries.
2. No brutalist buildings that Max adores have interesting geometries.
3. Every style that Max adores is either Zaha Hadid's design style or Kelly Wearstler's design style.
4. All of Kelly Wearstler's design styles that Max adores are evocative.
5. All of Kelly Wearstler's design styles that Max adores are dreamy.
6. If a design by Max that he adores has interesting geometries, then the design is a brutalist building and evocative.

Given these premises, let's analyze the possible scenarios for a design by Max that he adores:

- Since no brutalist buildings that Max adores have interesting geometries, a design that Max adores and has interesting geometries must be a Zaha Hadid design.
- From premise 6, if a design by Max that he adores has interesting geometries, it is a brutalist building and therefore evocative.
- Since all of Kelly Wearstler's design styles that Max adores are both evocative and dreamy, any design by Max that he adores and is a Kelly Wearstler design would be both evocative and dreamy.

However, the conclusion states that "A design by Max is evocative and dreamy." This must be true because, regardless of whether the design is a Zaha Hadid design (which only needs to be evocative as per the brutalist condition) or a Kelly Wearstler design (which is inherently both evocative and dreamy), the conclusion is satisfied. Therefore, the answer is True.
Processed: True

All of Kelly Wearstler's design styles that Max adores are evocative.
All of Kelly Wearstler's design styles that Max adores are dreamy.
If a design by Max that he adores has interesting geometries, then the design is a brutalist building and evocative.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
A design by Max is either evocative or dreamy.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
ANSWER: True

Let's break down the premises to understand why the conclusion follows:

1. **Premise 1:** All of Zaha Hadid's design styles that Max adores have interesting geometries.
2. **Premise 2:** No brutalist buildings that Max adores have interesting geometries.
3. **Premise 3:** Every style that Max adores is either Zaha Hadid's design style or Kelly Wearstler's design style.
4. **Premise 4:** All of Kelly Wearstler's design styles that Max adores are evocative.
5. **Premise 5:** All of Kelly Wearstler's design styles that Max adores are dreamy.
6. **Premise 6:** If a design by Max that he adores has interesting geometries, then the design is a brutalist building and evocative.

From Premises 1 and 2, we know:
- If a design has interesting geometries, it cannot be a brutalist building because no brutalist buildings that Max adores have interesting geometries.

From Premises 3, 4, and 5, since every style Max adores is either Zaha Hadid's or Kelly Wearstler's, and all Kelly Wearstler's designs that Max adores are both evocative and dreamy, we can conclude the following about a design by Max that he adores:
- If a design by Max has interesting geometries, it must be a brutalist building (by Premise 6).
- Since no brutalist buildings that Max adores have interesting geometries (Premise 2), it means Max's designs with interesting geometries do not exist.
- Therefore, every design by Max that he adores, being either a Zaha Hadid design or a Kelly Wearstler design, must be evocative or dreamy (since all Kelly Wearstler’s designs are both).

Given the above, we can conclude that any design by Max that he adores is either evocative or dreamy, as all of Kelly Wearstler’s designs that Max adores are both evocative and dreamy, and there is no way for a design to have interesting geometries without being a brutalist building (which cannot happen according to the premises). Thus, the conclusion "A design by Max is either evocative or dreamy" is true based on the given premises.

=== Example 42 ===
Prompt:
The following is a first-order logic (FOL) problem.
The problem is to determine whether the conclusion follows from the premises.
The premises are given in the form of a set of first-order logic sentences.
The conclusion is given in the form of a single first-order logic sentence.
The task is to evaluate the conclusion as ANSWER: True, ANSWER: False, or ANSWER: Uncertain given the premises.


<PREMISES>
All biodegradable things are environment-friendly.
All woodware is biodegradable.
All paper is woodware.
Nothing is a good thing and also a bad thing.
All environment-friendly things are good.
A worksheet is either paper or environment-friendly.

</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
A La Liga soccer team ranks higher than another La Liga soccer team if it receives more points.
If there are two La Liga soccer teams and neither has more points than the other, then the team which receives more points from the games between the two teams ranks higher.
Real Madrid and Barcelona are both La Liga soccer teams.
Real Madrid received more points than Barcelona.
Neither Real Madrid nor Barcelona received more points from the games between them.

<PREMISES>
All professional athletes spend most of their time on sports.
All Olympic gold medal winners are professional athletes.
No full-time scientists spend the majority of their time on sports.
All Nobel physics laureates are full-time scientists.
Amy spends the most time on sports, or Amy is an Olympic gold medal winner.
If Amy is not a Nobel physics laureate, then Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
If someone is ranked highly by the Women's Tennis Association, then they are one of the most active players in major tennis.
Everyone who lost to Iga Świątek at Roland Garros 2022 is ranked highly by the Women's Tennis Association.
All female tennis players at Roland Garros 2022 lost to Iga Świątek.
All tennis players at Roland Garros 2022 are either female or male.
All male tennis players at Roland Garros in 2022 lost to Rafael Nadal.
If Coco Gauff is ranked highly by the Women's Tennis Association or lost to Rafael Nadal, then Coco Gauff is not a male tennis player at Roland Garros 2022.
Coco Gauff is at Roland Garros 2022.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
Coco Gauff is among the most active Grand-Slam players.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
ANSWER: True

Let's break down the premises and analyze step-by-step:

1. If someone is ranked highly by the Women's Tennis Association, then they are one of the most active players in major tennis.
   - \( R(x) \rightarrow A(x) \)
   Here, \( R(x) \) means "x is ranked highly by the Women's Tennis Association" and \( A(x) \) means "x is one of the most active players in major tennis."

2. Everyone who lost to Iga Świątek at Roland Garros 2022 is ranked highly by the Women's Tennis Association.
   - \( L(x, Iga) \rightarrow R(x) \)
   Here, \( L(x, Iga) \) means "x lost to Iga Świątek at Roland Garros 2022."

3. All female tennis players at Roland Garros 2022 lost to Iga Świątek.
   - \( F(x) \land R(x, 2022) \rightarrow L(x, Iga) \)
   Here, \( F(x) \) means "x is a female tennis player," and \( R(x, 2022) \) means "x is at Roland Garros 2022."

4. All tennis players at Roland Garros 2022 are either female or male.
   - \( R(x, 2022) \rightarrow (F(x) \lor M(x)) \)
   Here, \( M(x) \) means "x is a male tennis player."

5. All male tennis players at Roland Garros 2022 lost to Rafael Nadal.
   - \( M(x) \land R(x, 2022) \rightarrow L(x, Rafa) \)
   Here, \( L(x, Rafa) \) means "x lost to Rafael Nadal."

6. If Coco Gauff is ranked highly by the Women's Tennis Association or lost to Rafael Nadal, then she is not a male tennis player at Roland Garros 2022.
   - \( (R(Coco) \lor L(Coco, Rafa)) \rightarrow \neg M(Coco) \)
   Here, \( L(Coco, Rafa) \) means "Coco Gauff lost to Rafael Nadal."

7. Coco Gauff is at Roland Garros 2022.
   - \( R(Coco, 2022) \)

Now, we need to check if Coco Gauff is among the most active Grand-Slam players.

From premise 3, since all female tennis players at Roland Garros 2022 lost to Iga Świątek, and Coco Gauff is at Roland Garros 2022:
- \( R(Coco, 2022) \rightarrow L(Coco, Iga) \)

From premise 2, since everyone who lost to Iga Świątek is ranked highly by the Women's Tennis Association:
- \( L(Coco, Iga) \rightarrow R(Coco) \)

From premise 6, if Coco Gauff is ranked highly by the Women's Tennis Association:
- \( R(Coco) \rightarrow (R(Coco) \lor L(Coco, Rafa)) \rightarrow \neg M(Coco) \)

Since Coco Gauff is not a male tennis player, from premise 5:
- \( \neg M(Coco) \)

Finally, from premise 1, since Coco Gauff is ranked highly by the Women's Tennis Association:
- \( R(Coco) \rightarrow A(Coco) \)

Therefore, Coco Gauff is among the most active Grand-Slam players. The answer is **True**.
Processed: True

Reference: True
========================================

- **Premise 2:** Some pets are not mammals.

From Premise 1, we know that any cat is included in the group of mammals. 

From Premise 2, we know there exist some pets that are not mammals. However, this doesn't provide information about whether these non-mammal pets include any cats or not.

Since Premise 1 states all cats are mammals, but Premise 2 only tells us that some pets are not mammals, it is possible for there to be cats that are also pets. This means that it is not necessarily true that no pets are cats.

Therefore, the conclusion "No pets are cats" cannot be logically inferred from the given premises. Hence, the answer is **False**.
Processed: False

Reference: Uncertain

</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
If Amy is not an Olympic gold medal winner, then Amy is a Nobel physics laureate.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>
ANSWER: False
</EVALUATE>

<PREMISES>
No digital media are analog.
Every printed text is analog media.
All streaming services are digital media.
If an object is a hardcover book, then it is printed text.
If 1984 is a streaming service, then 1984 is a hardcover book.
</PREMISES>
<CONCLUSION>
1984 is printed text.
</CONCLUSION>
<EVALUATE>

Generation 1:
ANSWER: True

Let's break down the premises step by step:

1. No digital media are analog. (¬(D → A))
2. Every printed text is analog media. (P → A)
3. All streaming services are digital media. (S → D)
4. If an object is a hardcover book, then it is printed text. (H → P)
5. If 1984 is a streaming service, then 1984 is a hardcover book. (S(1984) → H(1984))

Now let's see if we can conclude that 1984 is printed text.

- From premise 3, since 1984 is a streaming service, it follows that 1984 is digital media (S(1984) → D(1984)).
- From premise 1, no digital media are analog, so it cannot be true that 1984 is analog (D(1984) → ¬A(1984)).

Since 1984 is not analog, let's check if it could be printed text:

- Premise 2 states that every printed text is analog media, so for 1984 to be printed text, it would have to be analog. But we've already established that 1984 cannot be analog. Therefore, 1984 cannot be printed text.

However, the question asks specifically about the conclusion "1984 is printed text," and based on the premises, we can infer the opposite—1984 cannot be analog, and by premise 2, if something is not analog, it cannot be printed text.

Thus, the correct answer is that the conclusion "1984 is printed text" is false, but since the problem statement asks if the given conclusion is true, the logical evaluation here should indicate that the original conclusion is not supported by the premises, leading to the conclusion being false.

So, the final answer is:
ANSWER: False
Processed: True

Reference: Uncertain

### Reasoning:
Let's break down the premises and see if they logically lead to the conclusion that "1984 is a streaming service."

1. **No digital media are analog.**
2. **Every printed text is analog media.**
3. **All streaming services are digital media.**
4. **If an object is a hardcover book, then it is printed text.**
5. **If 1984 is a streaming service, then 1984 is a hardcover book.**
